## 0. Meta (read this header first)

- Repo: `mac-yolo-safeguards` (+ `hermes-mobile/` app, `~/.hermes` desktop agent — separate, not this repo)
- Updated: 2026-07-22 by `cursor-ts-watchdog-repair` (T-TS-WATCHDOG-SECRETLESS-20260722; coord T-NO-DESKTOP-HIJACK)
- Active agents (claim your id here): `cursor-profile-switch-bleed`, `cursor-ts-watchdog-repair`, `claude-code`, `cursor`, `antigravity`, `gemini`, `replit`, `cursor-mac-pro-picker`, `cursor-transport-ssot`, `cursor-stuck-wait`, `cursor-output-wipe`, `codex-thumbgate-feedback`, `codex-tinker-computer-use`, `terra-ci-ndk-pin`, `cursor-ts-vpn-detect`, `cursor-aso-listing-dominance`, `codex-aso-dominance-research`, `codex-usb-transport-preserve`, `grok-swarm-harness-roi`, `grok-authkit-max-age`, `terra-ota-rollout-clamp`, `cursor-thumbgate-promo-leash`, `cursor-no-desktop-hijack`
- Active branch of record: `main`
- Merge discipline: branch-per-agent → rebase onto `main` → **sequential** merge, gated on `npm test` + Maestro E2E (`hermes-mobile/docs/proofs/continuous/latest.json`).
- **THE RULES (see AGENTS.md "Multi-agent coordination" for the full Never-list):**
  - **Claim before you touch.** Add the file to §2 with your id+timestamp before editing it.
  - **Never edit a file another agent owns** in §2. If you need it → mark your task `blocked`, log it in §3, and **STOP** (no workarounds, no deleting their claim).
  - One agent per worktree/branch; serialize git ops.

- 2026-07-12 `codex-grok45-roi`: **T-159 CodeQL remediation and evidence correction.** CodeQL alert #32 correctly rejected fast SHA-256 task hashing as guessable sensitive-data handling. - 2026-07-12 `codex-grok45-roi`: **T-159 CodeQL second-pass correction.** CodeQL alert #33 still treated HMAC as password hashing because task text remained a cryptographic input. Final design removes that relationship entirely: legacy `*Digest` receipt fields now contain fresh random opaque ids; task/query/output text is neither hashed nor cached, so even repeated input in the same process is unlinkable. ## 4. Discovered Tasks (append-only inbox → promote into §1)

- 2026-07-22T17:15:00Z `cursor` (read-only investigation, no code edits — feeds T-STUCK-WAIT-HARD-TIMEOUT + T-TRANSPORT-LABEL-SSOT/T-MINI-STICKY-PROFILE owners): **Live-caught reproduction of "Connected+Waiting forever" + phantom-session 404 + Mac-mini mislabeled as MacBook-Pro, thread "Why we made zero dollars."** (1) **Client hard-timeout not firing in production**: 12:59 PM send "make money today" (session `mobile_1784665204206_b230283b`) showed "Waiting 3m 05s" then "Waiting 6m 11s" on-device (screenshots), blowing through `promptReplyElapsed.ts` `PROMPT_REPLY_HARD_TIMEOUT_MS=2min` with zero recovery/error — confirms T-STUCK-WAIT-HARD-TIMEOUT's target bug is real and currently unfixed on the installed build. (2) **Server-side root cause of that stall** (mini `~/.hermes/logs/agent.log`, `100.94.135.78`, ssh-verified): every turn on this session first calls an "NVIDIA NIM" auxiliary-compression provider that 401s (`resolve_provider_client: named custom provider 'NVIDIA NIM' has no resolvable api_key`), then falls through to the real generation on a local Ollama model (`qwen3.5:9b-hermes-64k`, NOT the "GLM Coding" label the header shows) against a ~65-73K-token context — one stream attempt took 12:59:46→13:05:32 (5m46s) before erroring/retrying (attempt 2/3 logged). Compounding 3x retries × ~6min each = 15-20min "Waiting" with no cap. (3) **Session/transport identity bugs**: `mobile_1784665204206_b230283b` does not exist in the MacBook Pro's `state.db` (0 rows) — it only exists on the Mac mini's `state.db` — yet the MacBook Pro gateway logged repeated 404s for `/api/sessions/mobile_1784665204206_b230283b/messages` from the phone (`~/.hermes/logs/agent.log` 12:51-12:52), i.e. the phone/relay polled the wrong host for a real session that lives elsewhere. Separately, `curl http://100.94.135.78:8642/health` (the mini) returns `"hostname": "Igors-MacBook-Pro.local"` — a real mislabel bug for T-TRANSPORT-LABEL-SSOT/T-MINI-STICKY-PROFILE to fix at the gateway/health-payload layer, not just the client label. (4) **Earlier 12:13 PM incident (same thread, MacBook Pro gateway) was a different flavor of the same class**: assistant bubble ended on "Let me activate processing on viable leads and show what's actually happening now:" with no tool call and no follow-up; full-text search of `state.db` (`content`, `api_content` columns) found **zero** rows containing that text anywhere — the visible bubble was never persisted server-side, consistent with a stream that partially rendered client-side then errored (litellm `proxy.err.log` shows repeated `opencode-go-glm` "Weekly usage limit reached" + "No fallback model group found for original model_group=opencode-go-glm" around the same window) before the write-to-transcript step. Client-side, `promptReplyElapsed.ts` `findSubstantiveAssistantReplyAfter` treats ANY non-empty assistant text as a completed turn (`mode: 'frozen'`) — so once partial text streamed, the live/stall watch permanently stood down and thumbs-up/down rendered, with no mechanism to detect "assistant announced further action via trailing colon but never delivered it." Recommend: (a) cap total NVIDIA-NIM-then-local retry loop wall-clock, not just per-attempt; (b) treat a `finish_reason` other than a real tool-call/stop-with-content, or any turn whose rendered text ends in an unresolved "let me do X:" with no subsequent tool_calls, as non-terminal for stall-detection purposes; (c) gateway `/health` hostname must reflect the actual machine, not a copied config value. No files edited (avoided all owners' claimed slices above); revenue funnel state (independent verification, `node tools/revenue-autonomous-loop.js --auto-send --json`, 2026-07-22T17:08Z): 21 sent / 2 lost / $15,481 open gross; 1 of 3 Stripe links live (`Agent Reliability Diagnostic` 200; `Partner Pilot` + `Hardening Sprint` both 403); Gmail API broken (traceback); `auto_send=blocked_by_safety_gate`, `sentCount=0` — real, separate contributor to "why we made zero dollars" beyond the stuck chat bubble.

- 2026-07-01 `claude-code`: **Root-cause hand-off for T-44 (@codex) — the primary-Mac override also lives in `GatewayContext.tsx`, not just ChatScreen auto-discovery.** Igor re-raised "users should be able to choose any machine as primary." Read-only trace (did NOT edit — file is gemini T-1 `DO NOT EDIT`): in `GatewayContext.tsx` `tryMacGatewayWithLoopbackFallback`, when the user's chosen Mac is briefly unreachable, the cross-machine `savedProfileFallbackUrls` loops call `persistDiscoveredGatewayUrl(fallbackUrl, /*makeActive*/ true)` (lines ~690 and ~739). That flows to `upsertDiscoveredProfile(..., makeActive=true)` → `activeProfileId = <fallback machine>` (`services/gatewayProfiles.ts:405/421`), **silently reassigning the user's primary to whatever Mac answered first.** So fixing only ChatScreen's on-select auto-discovery won't fully stop the override. Proposed fix (needs gemini sign-off since it's T-1's file): pass `makeActive=false` in the two cross-machine `savedProfileFallbackUrls` fallbacks so a transient fallback serves the request without hijacking the chosen primary; first-ever connect still auto-selects via the existing `|| !activeProfileId` guard at line ~605, and same-machine URL healing is unaffected (upsert matches the active profile by hostname/IP). @codex + @gemini coordinate scope. - 2026-07-07 `antigravity`: **Completed T-74 (Fix Leash tab infinite swipe-to-refresh spinner loop and release-safety test regex).** Root cause: in `ApprovalsScreen.tsx`, `onRefresh` depended on the `refreshing` state, while `useFocusEffect` callback depended on `onRefresh`. Thus, toggling `refreshing` re-created `onRefresh`, triggering `useFocusEffect` to re-run and launch a new refresh call, causing a permanent infinite refresh spinner loop on the Leash tab. Fix: decoupled `refreshing` from `onRefresh` via `refreshingRef`, and tracked `connectionState` inside the focus effect via `connectionStateRef`, eliminating the loop while keeping focus refresh intact. Also fixed a false release-safety test failure where the new gated E2E helper inside `install-phone-release.sh` was matched by the strict build-block regex; counted occurrences to verify flags are not unconditionally exported elsewhere. Verification: focused Jest `ApprovalsScreen.test.tsx` and `releaseSafetyContract.test.ts` pass, all 131 test suites / 1001 unit tests pass, typechecks pass, and continuous E2E ran with high-load skip recorded to `latest.json`.

### 2026-07-14 — Safe 9Router adoption without credential or routing drift
- **Finding:** Upstream 9Router 0.5.30 provides useful OpenAI-compatible routing and telemetry, but its CLI defaults to `0.0.0.0`, offers tunnel/MITM paths, and persists provider credentials in SQLite. A plain global install was not acceptable for Hermes.
- **Fix:** Added a pinned SHA-512 installer with npm lifecycle scripts disabled, direct 768 MB-capped server launch on `127.0.0.1:20128`, isolated `~/.hermes/9router` data, one secret-free local Ollama provider, safe settings, `9router-yolo`, and the explicit `hermes-9router` receipt route. Default `hermes-yolo` is untouched.
- **Proof:** Both focused tests pass; Mac Pro doctor ready at PID 50888 / 159 MB RSS and mini doctor ready at PID 60138 / 133 MB RSS; both listeners are exactly `127.0.0.1:20128`; both standalone markers and both `HERMES_9ROUTER_OK` executions passed; receipts are mode 0600; wrapper hashes match across hosts.
- **Decision:** Keep 9Router explicit/local-only until comparative harness eval proves that any cloud combo or RTK setting improves completion reliability without tool/schema regression or silent model switching.

### 2026-07-14 — Session-start submitted-job restart loop
- **Finding:** The reusable-label live proof showed `launchctl submit` infers KeepAlive: a successful phone install/pair command restarted 113 times, then disappeared. The earlier persistent disabled override was a symptom of that loop, not the root cause. A second session can also race a submitted service while its state is `spawn scheduled`, because the busy probe only recognized `state = running`.
- **Promoted:** T-315 now owns `tools/agent-phone-pipeline-lock.js` as well as the original session-start and contract-test files. The fix must self-remove the submitted service after one attempt and consider any present submitted service busy.

### 2026-07-14 — T-322 real-workload gate for local Hermes models
- **Finding:** T-320 selected models by installed name and status output, so it missed two runtime facts: the 8B profile launched at 40,960 context and crossed the freeze guard's 10 GiB worker class under pressure, while a first 20k mitigation was rejected by current Hermes Agent's hard 64k minimum. A nominal 3B/64k profile was also rejected after `ollama ps` proved Ollama clamped it to 32,768.

It unloads/disables the LiteLLM and hourly competence-probe bypasses and blocks direct `litellm` execution with the other provider commands.
- **Proof:** MacBook Pro / mini cold probes returned HTTP 200 for 12,365 prompt tokens with worker RSS 7,323,760 / 8,477,264 KiB; both freeze-guard passes preserved the same PIDs with no new `OLLAMA_RECLAIM`; real CLI runs returned `HERMES-LOCAL-CLI-OK` / `HERMES-MINI-CLI-OK`; gate SHA-256 `4cc9e5ed2aa92dd1c2fc19b6e70b07d75aa515e052002f9d4656b424201d313b` matched source and both installs; 19/19 paid/provider entrypoints on each host resolved to that gate and exited 73 before spawn.
- **Heuristic:** A local model is route-ready only after the live worker proves its actual context and RSS, a representative cold prompt completes, the host safeguard preserves the worker, and the real harness CLI passes. Model names, Modelfiles, and route-status JSON are not execution proof.

### 2026-07-14T20:45:00Z — `cursor` — Completed T-321 follow-up: P0 Send grayed after "Reply ready"
- **P0 report (16:14 EDT):** Phone screenshot showed "Reply ready on your computer" banner + Dismiss/Start-fresh-chat, but the Send button stayed grayed even after typing a new distinct message ("Make money faster").
- **Root cause:** the dead-run-unlock path in `ChatScreen.tsx` (T-321 CTA) cleared `isSending` but never cleared `pinnedOutboundStatus`/`pinnedOutboundText`/`queuedOutboundCount`. `ChatInputBar`'s `sendDisabled` includes `outboundSendStillPending` (`pinnedOutboundStatus === 'pending' && pinnedOutboundText`), so once a run was detected dead the composer stayed locked forever regardless of new typed text. A second contributing bug: `shouldSurfaceDeadRunEnded` gated on the *global* `/v1/obsidian/agents` count, so any unrelated scheduled job elsewhere on the Mac could permanently block dead-run detection for this session.
- **Fix (already open as PR #384, branch `fix/dead-run-send-unlock`, 3 commits by a prior session):** dead-run unlock now also resets `awaitingGatewayReply`, `activeOutboundSendBodyRef`, `pendingOutboundSendsRef`, `outboundQueueRef`/`queuedOutboundCount`, and `pinnedOutboundStatus`/`pinnedOutboundText`/`pinnedOutboundSentAt`; `shouldSurfaceDeadRunEnded` no longer takes `activeAgentCount`; `shouldBlockComposerSend` no longer blanket-blocks a **distinct** new message while busy (only dedupes exact re-sends).
- **Verification:** local `npm test -- --no-coverage --watchman=false` → 173 suites / 1448 tests pass (including new `isComposerSendDisabled` unlock-state regression tests). PR #384 CI green (required checks: Public funnel checks, Socket Security Project Report, Hermes Mobile typecheck+tests, **Maestro ship-guard (Android emulator)** 18m45s pass, macOS guard kit). Auto-merge (already enabled) merged PR #384 at `f68b932e` (2026-07-14T20:27:29Z). Production+preview OTA published for `f68b932e` at 20:37:44Z (`eas update:list --branch production` confirms group `6b8bb3fd-181c-46d5-96d5-8e62d51ae95d`, runtimeVersion `1.0`, matches `app.json` `version`). Repaired flaky USB twice via `node tools/hermes-mobile-pair.js` (adb reverse 8642/8765, `/api/sessions` 200). Device `R3CY90QPM7E` cold-started twice post-publish and reported `NoUpdatesAvailable` both times — confirms it is already serving the just-published production update (the fix), not a stale bundle.
- **No new bug beyond #384** — the reported symptom is fully explained by the two root causes above, both already fixed on the merged branch.

### 2026-07-14T18:40:00Z — `cursor-p0-empty-picker` — T-333 (renumbered from T-332): P0 "No machines found" — empty picker, both Macs actually healthy
- **P0 report (18:26 ET, screenshot):** Header `Computer via USB · USB Reconnecting` (red); "Choose your computer" modal showed **"No local Hermes machines found"** and **"No saved computers yet"** even though the MacBook Pro (USB) and Mac mini had both worked minutes earlier.
- **Root cause (found already in flight by a concurrent session, transcript `557af397`, and independently re-confirmed here):** T-330's secretless-pairing contract expects the deep link param **`pairCode=`**, but `tools/hermes-mobile-pair.js`'s `buildSecretlessDeepLink()` emitted **`code=`**. `parseSetupDeepLink()` requires `pairCode` (or legacy `code` only when no `gatewayUrl` is present) — the mismatch made the parsed result effectively empty, so `applySetupDeepLink` never persisted a gateway profile or seeded `tailnetProbeHosts`. With zero saved profiles and zero probe hosts, both "No saved computers" and "Find computers found 0" are explained by the **same single bug** — not a network outage. `tailscale status` on the MacBook Pro showed `igors-mac-mini` (`100.94.135.78`) `active` and `igors-macbook-pro-1` (`100.87.85.85`, self) `active`; direct `curl` to both `:8642/health` returned `200 {"status":"ok",...}` throughout the incident, proving the tailnet/gateways were never down.
- **Fix (PR #392, already authored/pushed by the concurrent session before this verification pass):** pair script now emits `pairCode=`; `setupDeepLink.ts` keeps backward compat for legacy `code=`+`pairServer` links with no `gatewayUrl`; `GatewayOpsSection.tsx` Repair link bounded to a 12s timeout via `connectEvents`/`retryGatewayBootstrap` so Tools can't spin forever on a future regression.
- **Live re-verification (this session, 18:31 ET, phone `R3CY90QPM7E`):** re-ran `node tools/hermes-mobile-pair.js` on the already-fixed branch; log showed the corrected `hermes://setup?pairCode=RMVAAKA2&pairServer=...` link and `Extra saved computer (verified auth): Igors-Mac-mini http://100.94.135.78:8642`. Fresh `adb screencap` immediately after shows the header flipped to green **`Igors-MacBook-Pro · USB Connected`**. PR #392 CI was green on all required checks except the ~18min `Maestro ship-guard (Android emulator)` (still in progress at verification time); PR #389 (unrelated T-331 mac-mini picker-filter fix) was also still `mergeStateStatus=BLOCKED` pending the same slow required check — both have GitHub auto-merge already enabled and will land as soon as that check completes, no manual action needed.
- **Heuristic:** when a "no machines found" report includes profiles that were saved and working minutes earlier, check the pairing/deep-link contract for a param-name mismatch before suspecting Tailscale/network — a single silently-dropped deep link can explain both "no saved computers" and "scan found 0" at once.

### 2026-07-14T18:52:00Z — `cursor-usb-hijack-guard` — T-334 P0: USB header showed Mac mini while phone was cabled to the MacBook Pro
- **P0 report (18:47 ET):** Phone `R3CY90QPM7E` USB-cabled to `Igors-MacBook-Pro`, but the app's USB row/header showed the Mac mini.
- **Live evidence:** `adb shell curl 127.0.0.1:8642/health` (the real adb-reverse loopback tunnel, routed to whichever Mac's `adb` process holds the cable) returned `hostname: "Igors-MacBook-Pro.local"` — the cable and app-level identity law in `chatMachineHeader.ts` (`isLiveUsbHealthIdentity` / `resolveMachineDisplayName`) were correct and unaffected. `adb shell curl 127.0.0.1:8765/pair.json` (served by `tools/hermes-mobile-pair.js`'s local pair-server, also reachable through the same reverse tunnel) returned `gatewayUrl: http://100.94.135.78:8642, hostname: "Igors-Mac-mini"` — written to disk 11 minutes earlier at 18:36:01.
- **Root cause:** `AGENTS.md`'s standing "Multi-Mac API keys" instruction tells agents to run `node tools/hermes-mobile-pair.js --mini-tailscale` (SSH-fetches the mini's key) with no `--no-serve` requirement. In `runPairMain()`, the `--mini-tailscale` branch (line ~500) unconditionally set `gatewayUrl` to the mini's Tailscale IP as **primary**, bypassing both (a) the loopback-preference block (`!args.has('--mini-tailscale')` guard) and (b) the existing "refuse mini as USB primary" throw (also gated `!args.has('--mini-tailscale')`). `skipPairAssetWrite` (added by PR #363/#392 for a related but narrower "no-serve mini-tailscale" case) only skipped the `pair.json` write + adb push when the caller passed **both** `--no-serve` **and** `--mini-tailscale`. A bare `--mini-tailscale` invocation — exactly what AGENTS.md instructs — passed neither guard and freely rewrote `pair.json`'s primary to the mini and pushed an adb deep link naming the mini, even while the live loopback tunnel (and `/health`) still correctly answered as the MacBook Pro. Two prior "no-serve" fixes (PR #363, #392) closed adjacent gaps but never closed this exact one, since the standing operational command never includes `--no-serve`.
- **Fix:** `tools/hermes-mobile-pair.js` now checks the **live cable fact**, not just flags: when `--mini-tailscale` is used, `usbPairing` + `reversed8642` are true, and `verifyGatewayAuthSync('http://127.0.0.1:8642', readLocalApiKey())` proves the phone is genuinely cabled to *this* Mac, `usbHijackGuardTripped` forces the same safe read-only behavior PR #363 already had for `--no-serve` — `pair.json` is left untouched and the adb deep-link push is skipped — regardless of whether `--no-serve` was passed. Escape hatch `--force-mini-usb-primary` preserved for a genuinely intentional repoint. `explicitGatewayUrl` (`--gateway-url=...`) is exempt — that's explicit human intent, not the ambient key-sync flag.
- **Immediate ops correction:** re-ran `node tools/hermes-mobile-pair.js --no-dev-unlock`; live re-check confirms `pair.json` and `127.0.0.1:8642/health` both now agree on `Igors-MacBook-Pro`, primary `http://127.0.0.1:8642`. Re-ran `node tools/hermes-mobile-pair.js --mini-tailscale` (no `--no-serve`) to reproduce the exact hijack path against the fixed script: log shows `USB guard: phone is USB-cabled to THIS Mac … refusing to make mini the USB primary`, `pair.json: preserved`, `adb: skipped`; live re-check confirmed `pair.json` was untouched (still MacBook Pro) after that run.
- **Verification:** `bash tests/test-hermes-mobile-pair.sh` 35/35 pass (2 new regression checks added); `cd hermes-mobile && npm test -- --no-coverage --watchman=false` 175 suites / 1473 tests pass, 0 failures.
- **Heuristic:** any tool invocation documented as a "standing command" in `AGENTS.md` must be safe by default against the current live device state — don't rely on callers remembering an extra flag (`--no-serve`) to avoid clobbering a phone's live session; gate on verified live facts (loopback auth), not on which flags were passed.

### 2026-07-15T02:55:00Z — `cursor-usb-self-heal-followup` — T-336 P0: RELAY resource_exhausted → resilient self-healing USB/Tailscale (follow-up ship)
- **Directive:** RELAY failed (resource_exhausted); ship one focused PR for resilient self-healing USB/Tailscale — USB flap watchdog on foreground, repair-link timeout (dedupe against #392/#393), pair failure must not wipe `gatewayProfiles`, tests + `npm test`.
- **Found in flight first:** #392 (T-333) already shipped the 12s repair-link timeout in `GatewayOpsSection.tsx`. #394 (T-335, `cursor-usb-self-heal-ship`) merged (`5616d1ba`) while this session was investigating — it already delivers the app-side foreground-heal reset (`shouldRunForegroundUsbHeal` + resetting the 30s/6×5s silent heal budget on `AppState` → `active`) and preserves `gatewayProfiles` on a failed **deep-link** pair (`evaluatePairDeepLinkApply` in the new `pairDeepLinkApply.ts`). Both T-335 and T-395 (leash header) rows in §1 were still `in_progress` despite their PRs having merged — corrected to `done` here with commit SHA evidence.
- **Second, distinct bug found (not covered by #394):** `SettingsScreen.tsx handlePair` — the *manual* "PAIR WITH COMPUTER" MOON-DUST code-entry flow (separate from the deep-link/QR flow #394 fixed) called `saveSettings({ connectionMode: 'relay', ... })` **before** attempting `completePair(pairCode)`. A failed relay pair (e.g. the RELAY `resource_exhausted` in the incident title) left `connectionMode` stuck on `'relay'` with no valid token — `bootstrapGateway`'s relay branch short-circuits and never even attempts USB/Tailscale profile discovery, so a perfectly healthy saved USB/Tailscale Mac silently became unreachable in-app until the user noticed and manually switched back in Settings. Reordered: `completePair` now runs first; settings (including `connectionMode: 'relay'`) are only persisted on success. Two regression tests added (`SettingsScreen.test.tsx`): failure leaves `saveSettings` uncalled, success persists `connectionMode: 'relay'`.
- **Mac-side USB flap watchdog:** the phone app cannot execute `adb reverse` on itself — only the Mac can. Added `tools/hermes-usb-reverse-watchdog.js` (LaunchAgent, 15s `StartInterval`) that reuses `hermes-mobile-pair-lib.js`'s existing `assertUsbAdbReverses`/`setupUsbAdbReverses` (no duplicated adb-parsing logic) to detect and re-apply dropped `tcp:8642`/`tcp:8765` reverse tunnels — the literal root cause diagnosed in the prior USB-flap incident. This complements #394's app-side health-probe reset (which retries reaching the gateway) by fixing the actual tunnel underneath it. Live-reproduced: `adb reverse --remove tcp:8765` then one watchdog poll re-applied it (`adb reverse --list` confirmed both ports live again).
- **Verification:** `npm test -- --no-coverage --watchman=false` 176 suites / 1482 tests pass; `npm run typecheck` clean; `node tests/test-hermes-usb-reverse-watchdog.js` 5/5 (stateful fake-adb fixture, no real device needed); `bash tests/test-hermes-mobile-pair.sh` 35/35 (unaffected — only imported, not modified); live on-device USB-flap reproduction on `R3CY90QPM7E`.
- **Heuristic:** before shipping a "resilience" P0 across USB/pairing, check `git log --oneline HEAD..origin/main` for the exact same task landing mid-session under a different task number — this repo runs 5-10+ concurrent agents and near-duplicate claims (T-332 vs T-333, two T-335 rows) are common; the mitigation is always to diff the *actual merged code* against the requested fix, not just the task title, to find the genuinely uncovered gap.

### 2026-07-15T03:30:00Z — `cursor-connect-gate-verify` — T-338 verification + duplicate PR #401 closed in favor of #399
- **User report (10:38 PM ET, screenshot):** `ConnectMacGate` had no visible Close/Not-now (`isDemoModeAllowed()` is dev/E2E/store-review only, so real production users had zero way out — a genuine full-screen modal trap), a "Found 2 local Hermes machines" banner promised tappable rows that never rendered (`LanScanResult` only carries a `foundCount`, no machine identities, and `ConnectMacGate` never cross-referenced the freshly-upserted `gatewayProfiles`), and onboarding step 1 said "Same home Wi‑Fi" unconditionally, including on cellular.
- **Found already in flight:** by the time this session reached `ConnectMacGate.tsx`, `cursor-connect-mac-gate-p0` had already authored and pushed the complete fix as PR #399 (branch `fix/connect-mac-gate-trap-ux`, commit `8d77ca67`) — "Not now" dismiss (tap **and** Android hardware back via `BackHandler`) persisting `settings.connectMacGateDismissed`, tappable found-machine rows via the existing shared `GatewayProfilePicker` (fed by `profilesForSwitchComputerPicker`, falling back to `profilesForDevicePicker`), and 3-step cellular-first onboarding copy ("Use Tailscale from cellular") replacing "Same home Wi‑Fi" when `wifiConnected === false`.
- **Duplicate found:** a second, independent open PR (#401, branch `fix/connect-mac-gate-dismiss`, opened the same minute as #399 from the same shared main worktree) targeted the identical file set with an equivalent fix, plus unrelated bundled diffs (T-333/T-334/USB-reverse-watchdog content that had already merged separately via #392/#393/#396) — a genuine race, not a superset. Running both auto-merges concurrently risked a conflict/no-op merge. Closed #401 with an explanatory comment pointing to #399 (branch/commits preserved, not deleted).
- **This session's contribution:** verified PR #399 end-to-end rather than re-implementing — read the actual pushed commit content (`git show 8d77ca67:...`) to confirm the fix was complete, watched full CI to green (all suites, `Hermes Mobile typecheck and tests`, `Reassure perf regression`, `macOS guard kit`, CodeQL `Analyze (swift)` 13m56s, and `Maestro ship-guard (Android emulator)` 19m7s — a real device-automation pass, not a skip), and confirmed auto-merge landed clean after a rebase-onto-main conflict (another concurrent agent resolved it live in the same worktree — observed but did not touch mid-merge) at `bf60bc1f` (2026-07-15T03:26:42Z). Kicked `com.igor.hermes-mobile-continuous-e2e`; `mobile-ota.yml` auto-triggered on the `main` push.
- **How the user closes the screen now:** tap **Not now** (top-right of the card, next to the title) — or, on Android, press the hardware Back button. Either dismisses the gate immediately and reveals Chat underneath; the choice persists (`connectMacGateDismissed: true`) so it will not re-trap on the next screen render. Silent background auto-heal (Find-computers retry loop, Tailscale probing) keeps running even while dismissed, and the gate resets/re-offers itself automatically once the phone actually connects.
- **Heuristic:** when a P0 report names the exact component and this repo shows 5-10+ concurrent agents, `git worktree list` + `gh pr list --search <keyword>` before writing any new code — the fix, and sometimes a duplicate of the fix, may already be mid-flight; the highest-leverage action is verification + duplicate-resolution, not a third parallel implementation.
